Local News

Rickshaw Pullers in the French Concession Clash with Vietnamese Police Yesterday – Twelve Injured, One Missing, Three Vietnamese Police Injured – Over 40,000 Rickshaw Pullers Strike, Rickshaws Disappear from Shanghai South

Over 40,000 rickshaw pullers in the Shanghai West and Shanghai South districts of this city, in opposition to registration by the French Concession, suddenly declared a general strike yesterday morning, clashing with Vietnamese police. One rickshaw puller is missing, twelve were injured, and three Vietnamese police were also injured. There were also incidents of tires being deflated along the way. Party and government organs, as well as Du Yuesheng, mediated again, but without effect. The trade association will hold a representatives' meeting today, and the rickshaw pullers will petition today, worsening the situation. Details are as follows:

General Strike

Over 40,000 rickshaw pullers in the French Concession, in opposition to the registration by the French Municipal Council, had repeatedly held meetings to protest. Mediation by party and government organs, as well as Du Yuesheng and others, proved ineffective due to the French authorities' firm stance and refusal to change the registration principles. Therefore, at a representatives' meeting the night before last, it was decided to declare a general strike at 6:00 AM yesterday morning as an effective countermeasure. The trade association tried to prevent it, but to no avail.

Clash Occurs

At 9:00 AM yesterday morning, over 1,500 representatives of the striking rickshaw pullers set off in a group from the Great South Gate to petition the city Party headquarters, the Chinese Ratepayers' Association of the French Concession, the police department, the Municipal Council, and the Second Special District Citizens' Association. Unexpectedly, when they reached Xie Bridge, Vietnamese police prevented the rickshaw pullers from passing. A verbal argument ensued, and the Vietnamese police then fired shots into the air as a warning. The rickshaw pullers, angered and agitated, clamored loudly, and the Vietnamese police used guns to beat and drive the rickshaw pullers away, resulting in many injuries. Three cars from the Lou Jia Wan police station, with both Chinese and foreign police, rushed into the Chinese territory.

Injured Rickshaw Pullers

As a result of the clash, rickshaw puller representative Xue San (also known as Ru Ji) is missing and has not been found as of late at night. The injured are: (1) Zhang Jia-mang (32 years old, from Taizhou, head and waist injuries); (2) Han Chang-sheng (28 years old, from Dongtai, leg and waist injuries). The above two are seriously injured and are at the Shanghai Hospital at the San Tai Wharf. (3) Zhao Zheng-yu (18 years old, from Taixing, head injury); (4) Wu Jin-fa (35 years old, from Yancheng, hand injury); (5) Chen Xi-wen (42 years old, from Taixian, head injury); (6) Lu Wen-sheng (34 years old, from Fu Rong, chest injury); (7) Lou Ai-shu (36 years old, from Taixian, waist injury); (8) Li Zi-qing (32 years old, from Fu Ning, head injury); (9) Hu Wen-sheng (22 years old, from Yancheng, leg injury); (10) Ma Yi-qing (36 years old, from Fu Ning, chest injury); (11) Tang Fu-yin (43 years old, from Fu Ning, head injury); (12) Wang An-sheng (19 years old, from Yancheng, chest injury). The above ten were bandaged and discharged from the hospital.

Vietnamese Police Cross the Border

At that time, the head Vietnamese police officer No. 173, along with police officers No. 223 and No. 440, crossed the border to pursue the rickshaw pullers, resulting in the loss of a pistol, No. 245644, belonging to police officer No. 170 of the Er Dao Tou and a rifle, No. 11414, belonging to a Chinese police officer, as well as eight bullets, during the chaos. They were later found by police officers from the Ximen Branch at the intersection of Lu Jia Bang and Lin Yin Road and retrieved by the French police station with a letter. At the time, three Vietnamese police officers were beaten and sent to the Guangci Hospital for treatment. During the clash, trams on lines 10, 6, 17, and 18 of the French Concession were blocked. The glass and other parts of tram No. 20 on line 6 were smashed.

Discussing Response

Because of the tragedy, the rickshaw pullers were filled with indignation and immediately convened an emergency representatives' meeting. It was decided to send six representatives – Xu Hongsheng, Zhou Yongcai, Li A-si, Zhou Li, Yang Yougui, and Wu Yigao – to lead 800 other representatives to petition various party and government organs and French Concession community organizations in the afternoon, demanding: (1) cancellation of registration; (2) punishment of the perpetrators; (3) compensation for losses. However, due to insufficient time to prepare the petition and other procedures, the petition was postponed to this morning.

Requesting Negotiations

After the strike broke out yesterday morning, rickshaw owners reported to the trade association, requesting serious negotiations with the French authorities. Therefore, the association specially sent executive members Qiu Chunshan, Zhang Huaiyang, and Song Yaokun to report the situation to Du Yuesheng, the Chinese director of the French Municipal Council, requesting renewed mediation. After the tragedy occurred at 9:00 AM, Yu Dajin was also sent to see Du Yuesheng, requesting that he stop the violence. Du Yuesheng agreed to visit the French consul to seek correction. As a result, the French consul believed that with three police officers injured, there was no room for reversal.

French Consul Negotiates

After the incident, Baudesson, the acting French Consul-General in Shanghai, drove to the city center at 11:30 AM to visit Mayor Wu Tiecheng and make representations. However, Mayor Wu stated that he would thoroughly investigate the rickshaw pullers' petition and the Vietnamese police's shooting before deciding on a concrete plan of action.

Party and Government Investigation

Upon receiving the report, party and government organs, considering the seriousness of the situation, sent Cao Peizi and Dai Youheng, staff members from the civil training section of the city Party headquarters, and Zhu Guilin, a mediator from the third section of the Social Affairs Bureau, to the scene of the incident, the trade association hospital, and the Public Security Ximen Branch at 2:00 PM yesterday afternoon to investigate the truth. The rickshaw pullers knelt before the party and government representatives, begging for negotiations. The three representatives agreed to investigate and report for instructions.

Owners Beaten

Because the negotiations had not yielded results, the rickshaw pullers vented their anger on Qiu Chunshan and Zhang Huaiyang, executive members of the trade association, for their ineffective handling of the matter. The night before last, they beat the executive members at the material distribution department of the association on San Guan Tang Road. At the same time, many rickshaw owners were beaten by the rickshaw pullers, and they reported to the trade association, strongly protesting to the French police to prevent the owners from being innocently humiliated.

Trade Association Meeting

The trade association, considering the seriousness of the situation, decided to hold a meeting of rickshaw owners at the Municipal Chamber of Commerce at 8:00 AM this morning to discuss countermeasures. The announcement stated: "Regarding the French Concession's rickshaw registration incident, all mediation efforts have been ineffective. From today, the rickshaw pullers will refuse to pull rickshaws and will unanimously cease work. The losses to the rickshaw owners are enormous. In order to discuss countermeasures, a general meeting of rickshaw owners will be held at the Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce auditorium at the Tian Hou Gong Bridge at 8:00 AM tomorrow (i.e., August 7th) to discuss all courses of action. We hope that you will attend on time." According to a certain rickshaw owner, the rickshaw owners hope that the rickshaw pullers can resume work and register today. As for the registration fee of five jiao, the French Municipal Council has, in principle, agreed to reduce it, but the amount of the reduction has not yet been determined. Regardless of whether the amount is reduced or not, the rickshaw owners can be responsible for paying it in advance, which will be repaid by the rickshaw pullers in the future. Alternatively, if the French Municipal Council decides not to charge a registration fee in the future, the registration fees that have already been paid will be fully refunded. However, there can be no restrictions on the registration time, or if it must be restricted, it must be extended (according to the current regulations of the French Concession, the registration period is from July 10th to the end of the year, and the rickshaw owners suggest that it should be extended to the end of June next year).

Forced Deflation

Yesterday morning, after the rickshaw pullers in the French Concession went on strike, rickshaws disappeared from the roads within the concession and in Xiao Zhao Hui in the Nanshi area. Rickshaws from the Public Concession flocked to the Nanshi area to operate. Upon hearing the news, the striking rickshaw pullers sent out many people to order the deflation of the tires of the rickshaws. As a result, trams and public buses operated by Chinese merchants, as well as trams and public buses operated by French merchants, saw their business triple.

Owners' Statement

According to the person in charge of the rickshaw owners' association yesterday, since the entire body of rickshaw pullers unanimously protested and expressed opposition to the French Concession's rickshaw registration, the rickshaw owners, in addition to mediating, have conveyed the rickshaw pullers' demands and have been running around negotiating and appealing for help. Thanks to the mediation of representatives from the Social Affairs Bureau and the Public Utilities Bureau, as well as Mr. Du Yuesheng, but the French Concession authorities insisted on the established methods and refused to adopt public opinion or make appropriate revisions. They also used high-pressure tactics, seizing large numbers of rickshaws, detaining them in police stations, and using police vehicles to capture rickshaw pullers along the way and force them to register. These harsh measures not only disregarded our national sovereignty but also directly treated our Chinese people as slaves of a conquered nation. The association is heartbroken to witness this situation. The rickshaw owners have consistently advised the rickshaw pullers to wait patiently for mediation. At 3:00 PM yesterday (the 5th), the association reported the progress of the negotiations to the rickshaw pullers on San Guan Tang Road and again advised the rickshaw pullers to remain calm and make concessions in the spirit of prioritizing harmony. Unexpectedly, some rickshaw pullers were unable to understand the association's painstaking efforts to seek compromise and safeguard the overall situation, and they even beat the association's executive members Zhang Huaiyang and Qiu Chunshan on the spot, which is deeply regrettable. The association's two executive members, Zhang and Qiu, believe that their suffering is a sacrifice for the public good, and the rickshaw pullers who resorted to violence did so because they were forced by livelihood issues, which is understandable, so they have expressed their unwillingness to pursue the matter in order to show the rickshaw owners' and rickshaw pullers' sincere cooperation. However, the rickshaw pullers, considering their own livelihood and to help the rickshaw pullers who were forced to become unemployed, unanimously refused to pull rickshaws from this morning to show their resistance. The first to bear the brunt is the rickshaw owners. It is estimated that the rickshaw owners will suffer losses of 5,000 to 6,000 yuan per day of the strike. In addition to urging Mr. Du Yuesheng to continue to mediate, the association also advises the rickshaw pullers to resume work as soon as possible so that traffic between the Chinese and French areas will not be affected. However, the association will not be responsible for any unexpected actions taken by the rickshaw pullers during this strike due to excessive pressure.

Zhabei Silk Factory Resumes Work - A Few Workers South of the Railway Have Not Entered the Factory - Full Resumption of Work Expected from Today

According to the Central News Agency, the eighteen silk factories in the Zhabei area, after the strike that began on the morning of the 3rd, had the details of the investigation promptly dispatched by party and government organs. It was originally scheduled to resume work uniformly yesterday morning, but some workers in the silk factories south of the railway had not yet entered the factory yesterday morning. The capital side hopes that this matter can be resolved as soon as possible, as the silk factories have suffered from the impact of the economic downturn in recent years and are showing signs of decline. The silk industry is slightly better this year than in previous years. If both labor and capital can overcome difficulties together and cooperate wholeheartedly, the future of the silk industry may be saved. The party and government authorities are currently making every effort to mediate, and it is likely that full resumption of work will be achieved starting today.

Guangdong and Tianjin Press Circles Telegraph the Central Government - for Reconsideration and Amendment of the Publication Law - Shanghai Daily Press Association Unanimously Agrees

Since the amendment to the Publication Law was passed by the Legislative Yuan, news circles in various places have felt that it imposes too many restrictions and is unlikely to be implemented. They have repeatedly telegraphed the central government, requesting that principles be reconsidered and referred for reconsideration. The Shanghai Daily Press Association yesterday received a telegram from the press circles of Guangdong and Tianjin, expressing their sympathy and unanimous agreement in order to achieve the goal of reconsideration. The two telegrams are recorded separately below:

Tianjin

Shanghai Daily Press Association, the Ma telegram has been received. The new Publication Law is strictly restrictive and has many obstacles. It is unconventional and does not conform to public opinion. It is difficult to remain silent. Your association is following the requests of colleagues in various places and making firm and powerful claims. The news has spread, and everyone sympathizes. In addition to telegramming the Central Political Council, requesting that it accept public opinion, reconsider the principles, and refer them to the Legislative Yuan for reconsideration, we hereby reply. Tianjin Newspaper Trade Association bows, Trap.

Guangdong

Shanghai Daily Press Association to all newspapers, news agencies, and publishing circles nationwide, We hereby transmit a telegram to the National Government, which reads, "To the National Government, The Legislative Yuan has passed the amended Publication Law, which has many changes compared to the current law. Colleagues in various places have requested a delay in promulgation. The association has also held a meeting and believes that with the amended draft, the competent authorities in the publishing industry, the county government, or the Social Affairs Bureau directly under the Executive Yuan, have the power to detain and punish. We dare not be sure that they will be fair, which is enough to give corrupt officials the power to control public opinion and obliterate social justice. Furthermore, both Article 14 of the current law and the same article of the amended draft stipulate that corrections or rebuttals should be published in full and should correspond to the original text. This has always been the most difficult thing for the news industry. Now the amendment maintains the status quo without improvement. In the future, the pages of newspapers will be filled with lengthy corrections or rebuttals, losing their function, which is not the government's intention to support the news industry. Furthermore, the newly added Article 21 of the amended draft, "Private or family privacy events shall not be published," has a vague meaning and lacks clear standards. If an individual's behavior affects social order, then the person's good and evil deeds should be recorded and criticized by society in good faith. If all publications are prohibited, it will only encourage the evil habits of traitors and criminals and will not help to conceal evil and promote good. As for the third chapter, which stipulates inspection measures for books and other publications, newspapers are not mentioned, leading to nowhere to turn. Inspections and detentions vary from place to place. News operators have lost their principles to follow, and those who implement it have no standards, which will inevitably plunge the national news industry into a state of dying, and the future of culture is unthinkable. After careful consideration, we believe that it is difficult to implement. In addition to jointly requesting the Central Political Council to formulate new principles and submit them to the Legislative Yuan for reconsideration, we hereby telegraphically submit to your government, respectfully requesting a delay in promulgation in order to maintain the freedom of speech and publication, which is for the public good. Guangdong Press Association, Guangdong Provincial Journalists Association Joint Committee, Guangzhou Journalists Association, Trap," We hereby transmit this message, hoping that everyone will agree and achieve this goal. Guangdong Press Association, Guangdong Provincial Journalists Association Joint Committee, Guangzhou Journalists Association, Trap.

Overseas Chinese Affairs Bureau - Issues Funds to Assist Overseas Chinese - Three Yuan Per Person Distributed at the Jiangxi Guild Hall - Overseas Chinese from Wenzhou Scheduled to Return Home Tonight by Ship

Seventy-four overseas Chinese, including Hu Junmin, who were forced to return from Japan, have been petitioning the Municipal Government's Overseas Chinese Affairs Bureau and other organs for days due to livelihood difficulties, requesting assistance. The Overseas Chinese Affairs Bureau, out of concern for the overseas Chinese, specially issued temporary relief funds of three yuan per person yesterday. The overseas Chinese are scheduled to return to their hometown tonight by ship. The following are the details obtained by the reporter of the Industrial and Commercial Society:

Government Assistance

Because of their livelihood difficulties, the overseas Chinese went to the Overseas Chinese Affairs Bureau to request assistance. The bureau considered this matter to be of great importance and telegraphed the Central Overseas Chinese Affairs Commission for instructions. According to Liu Zhuchu of the bureau, the bureau originally had a temporary fee of five yuan per person to assist unemployed overseas Chinese returning to the country, but due to financial constraints, it stopped issuing them in March. However, Chen Shuren, Chairman of the Overseas Chinese Affairs Commission, believed that the current situation was special, so he instructed the bureau to approve the issuance of three yuan per person as temporary relief.

Distribution of Funds

After receiving the order, the Overseas Chinese Affairs Bureau specially appointed Tan Zhonglu, Hou Can, and Lin Zhaohong to take the funds to the Jiangxi Guild Hall in Dong Jia Du and distribute them according to the name list. The Municipal Public Security Bureau also sent a police officer to take care of the scene. The distribution started at 2:00 PM and ended at 5:00 PM. It is reported that after the Municipal Government received the overseas Chinese' request for assistance, it ordered the representative Hu Junmin to go to collect it this morning.

Returning Home Tonight

After receiving assistance from the Overseas Chinese Affairs Bureau, the overseas Chinese planned to return to their hometowns immediately. However, the travel expenses were huge, and they hesitated. They were given certificates by the Overseas Chinese Affairs Bureau to purchase half-price tickets as a gesture of preferential treatment. It is estimated that 51 people from Wenzhou will return to their hometowns by the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company's Haiyan ship tonight. Several dozens of people will go to Nanjing and Ningbo to seek a living.

Merchant Ships on the South China Route - Seeking Shelter from the Wind Midway

The China Merchants Steam Navigation Company's new ship, Hai Heng, sailed out of Hong Kong at 9:00 PM on the 2nd, heading back to Shanghai. After leaving Hong Kong, it encountered a hurricane along the way. It had to choose a safe place to anchor and seek shelter from the wind outside Shantou Port for two days and nights. Now that the wind has passed, it is sailing to Shanghai. The Haili ship left Shanghai for Hong Kong and Guangdong on the evening of the 3rd of this month, but when the ship reached the waters of Baiquan Island and Bullock, it encountered a hurricane. The Haili did not dare to risk sailing and immediately stopped sailing to seek shelter from the wind. After the wind passed, it sailed to the Eastson waters and encountered another hurricane, which was more severe. The Haili ship stopped sailing again and sent a telegram to Shanghai, waiting for the hurricane to pass before planning to sail forward again. Therefore, all merchant ships traveling back and forth on the South China route were affected by this hurricane.

Loan for the West Bao Section of the Longhai Railway - Approved for Installment Payments Starting in November - Banks Have Negotiated the Amount of Recognition

According to Xin Sheng News Agency, the Ministry of Railways, in order to construct the Xi'an-Baoji section of the Longhai Railway, borrowed 4.86 million yuan from the Bank of Communications, the Bank of Shanghai, the Bank of China, the Jincheng Bank, and the Continental Bank in Shanghai. A contract was signed long ago, stipulating an annual interest rate of 10%, and it was agreed that the loan would be paid in four installments starting in November. Repayment of principal would begin in June of the following year, with a term of four years, and the principal and interest would be fully paid off by the end of May 1940. As for the collateral, it is (1) the income from the sale of Longhai Railway tickets throughout the line by the China Travel Service, (2) the income from the transportation of coal by the Zhongxing Coal Mine Company and the Kai'ao Coal Mine Company on the Longhai Railway throughout the line. Although the total amount has been stipulated, the amount of recognition by each bank has been properly distributed by the syndicate organized by the above banks. Now the Xi'an to Xianyang section has started construction, and the Xianyang to Baoji section has been surveyed. It is expected that the Xi'bao section will be completed and open to traffic by the end of May next year. Now, Zeng Shenming, Vice Minister of the Ministry of Railways, has contacted the syndicate and has approved that the payments will start in November, according to the contract.

Siamese rice has long disappeared in Shanghai. However, the Siamese government is arrogant and stubborn. Not only has the treatment of our overseas Chinese not improved, but it has intensified the oppression, and harsh regulations have been added. Post Office Notice: Procedures for Inspecting Parcels for Mailing

Shanghai Postal Administration Notice No. 1244 states: It has been determined that from August 1st of this year, customs will cease inspecting domestic parcels at the time of mailing. However, parcels destined for the Three Eastern Provinces and Jehol, as well as parcels containing the following items, must still be inspected by customs before they can be mailed. This is hereby announced for general knowledge. The list is as follows: 1. Hypodermic syringes and needles; 2. Narcotics; 3. Films; 4. Radio equipment; 5. Cigarettes and tobacco, etc.; 6. Cigarette-making tools; 7. Revenue stamps and tax bills; 8. Silver bars and silver fragments; 9. Gold; 10. Military supplies; 11. Sodium hydride.

Private Shipbuilding Industry: Wage Reduction Dispute Resolved, Workers Have All Resumed Work

Due to poor business conditions in the private shipbuilding yards in Pudong recently, it was announced on August 1st that workers' wages would be reduced uniformly by 15 cents per day. Upon hearing this news, the workers were alarmed due to the impact on their livelihoods. After unsuccessful negotiations, they petitioned the Party and government authorities for mediation. The Social Affairs Bureau, upon receiving the petition, convened a mediation session yesterday, attended by Dai Youheng from the Municipal Party Headquarters, Song Anjia from the General Labor Union, Fang Changgen from the Coal and Right Barge Transportation Association, Ye Zhushan from the Private Shipbuilding Association, Chen Anjin and Lu Dafu from the Private Ship Woodworkers Union, etc. The meeting was chaired by Tan Peiyan from the Social Affairs Bureau. As a result of the mediation, three agreements were signed: 1. Wages will be reduced by 4 cents per day from the original wage rate; 2. The labor-management agreement signed in 1920 will remain valid for another three years; 3. This agreement will be valid for one year. Both parties expressed satisfaction, and a resolution was declared. The workers also resumed work yesterday.

The National Economic Council Re-assigns Wu Juenong to Investigate the European Tea Industry; Expected Return Next Spring

Xu Shiying: Drafts Fundamental Suggestions for Flood Control; Lengthy Document of Tens of Thousands of Words to Be Submitted to the Central Government Soon; If Implemented, Hopes to Permanently Eliminate Floods

According to the Dagong News Agency, our country suffers from severe floods and droughts every year, and the government and the people are engaged in rescue efforts, almost exhausting themselves. Xu Shiying, Chairman of the Central Relief Committee, has returned from inspecting the disaster situation in the Yangtze River provinces this year. In addition to submitting an inspection report and detailed relief measures to the Central Government, he has also drafted a proposal for short-term and long-term disaster relief measures based on his observations. The document is tens of thousands of words long and will be submitted to the Central Government for adoption after it is finalized. The key points are to allocate funds for water conservancy projects and to control floods for disaster prevention. The details are as follows:

Xu Shiying's Proposal for Flood Control and Disaster Prevention

Xu Shiying, Chairman of the Central Relief Committee, in view of the vast territory of our country, the crisscrossing rivers and lakes, and the lack of proper water management, almost every province suffers from floods and droughts every year. When disasters occur, people rush to rescue and provide temporary assistance. This year, the Yellow River and the Yangtze River have again overflowed. Engaging in disaster relief is certainly an urgent task at present. In addition to these short-term measures, to plan for the future and permanently avoid disasters, it is necessary to plan ahead and develop fundamental policies for flood control and disaster prevention. Therefore, after returning to Shanghai, Xu has been thinking deeply and carefully, and to the best of his knowledge, has personally drafted a disaster relief proposal with both short-term and long-term measures. According to the Dagong News Agency reporter, the key points of the proposal are that there are numerous water conservancy agencies in our country. The government should be requested to allocate large sums of money to supervise the water conservancy agencies to recruit water conservancy experts, actively carry out water conservancy projects, dredge rivers and lakes, divert the Huai River into the sea, open up tributaries, and use the relief funds after the disaster for water management to prevent future disasters, while also benefiting agricultural irrigation. The document is tens of thousands of words long and presents thorough arguments.

Submitted to the Central Government for Adoption and Implementation

The content of the proposal is based on Xu's years of experience in disaster relief and his investigation into the causes of floods and droughts. It lists various short-term and long-term measures, along with notes on opinions and reasons. Because the full text is tens of thousands of words long, it has not yet been fully finalized. Xu told the Dagong News Agency reporter yesterday that the various water management plans in the proposal may seem idealistic at first glance, but they are all based on reasons and evidence, and they refer to frequent disasters in recent years, which are factual problems. He firmly believes that if this proposal can be implemented, it can permanently eliminate floods. The full text will be submitted to the Central Government for adoption as soon as it is finalized in the coming days, but because the content is of great importance, it will not be released to the public for the time being.

Sichuan Province Implements Unified Tax; Shanghai-Based Sichuan Merchants Request Strict Prohibition of Over-Collection; Unified Tax Implemented from August 1st

The Shanghai Sichuan Merchants Public Welfare Association, in response to the implementation of the unified tax in Sichuan Province starting this month, telegraphed the Chongqing Chamber of Commerce and the Sichuan Provincial Government, requesting them to pay attention to tax officials so as not to cause over-collection of local taxes. The two telegrams are as follows: (1) Chongqing Chamber of Commerce, Cotton Yarn and Piece Goods Industry Association, Greetings. Our Sichuan has suffered from over-collection for a long time. The Central Government and the Sichuan Provincial Government have negotiated to designate this province as a unified tax zone. The Ministry of Finance has issued an order stating that goods entering the province that have already been subject to the unified tax will be exempt from local taxes, and it is limited to implementation from August 1st. The cotton yarn and its woven products entering Sichuan should be subject to the unified tax from August 1st, and local taxes should be stopped. It can be seen that the central and local authorities are determined to reform Sichuan's administration and show consideration for the difficulties of merchants. However, the tax system relies on implementation. From that day forward, if any goods that have been transported to Chongqing and have completed the unified tax are found to be over-collected local taxes under any pretext, we hope that your association will lead the various industries to fight for it in accordance with the order and do not relax in the slightest. This matter concerns the public welfare of Sichuan merchants. In addition to telegraphing the Provincial Government to strictly prohibit over-collection of local taxes, we specially telegraph this notice. Please indicate the situation after the implementation of the unified tax. Shanghai Sichuan Merchants Public Welfare Association; (2) Telegram to the Chengdu Provincial Government, Greetings. Our Sichuan will implement the unified tax from August 1st and stop collecting local taxes, showing your government's willingness to consult with the central government, reform Sichuan's administration, and show consideration for the difficulties of merchants. However, good tax relies on implementation. We sincerely fear that local officials may not be able to fully appreciate the government's virtue when tax laws change, and may over-collect local taxes on goods that have already completed the unified tax. Please strictly prohibit it. Sichuan is fortunate, and Sichuan merchants are fortunate. Shanghai Sichuan Merchants Public Welfare Association.

Throwing Red Pills to Frame the Head of the Tu Dong

Gu Zhongyu, who lives at No. 50 Shigen Lane, Hongqiao Road, West Shanghai, is currently the head of the Tu Dong and squad leader of the Security Defense Post in the 29th Bao, Pushong District. He recently had a dispute over land sales in the countryside with his cousin Gu Fuquan, who is a carpenter. They filed a lawsuit in court and accumulated hatred. The next morning (22nd) at around 8:00 AM, Gu Fuquan reported to the relevant Pushong Police Station that Gu Zhongyu was selling drugs. The director believed that the statements were contradictory and sent a document to the Shanghai Municipal Public Security Bureau for transfer to the Songhu Garrison Headquarters for thorough investigation to clarify the truth. Since the incident occurred, the people in the West Shanghai area have been discussing it and felt unfair. Lu Ying, the chief of the detective team of the Municipal Public Security Bureau, and Ji Puyuan, the deputy chief, also paid close attention to it. They sent Gu Liancheng, the squad leader, to the countryside for secret investigation. It was not until the night before last that ten true facts were obtained. Chen Aping and Wang Gensheng, accomplices of Gu Fuquan, were arrested, and Wang Xinggao (also known as Wang Jianqiu) had escaped. They were taken back to the team for strict questioning. After obtaining the confession, the team leader submitted it to the Municipal Public Security Bureau for transfer to the Songhu Garrison Headquarters for trial.

The Conclusion of the Zhou Ruiqing's Tragic Death Case

Zhou Ruiqing from Yancheng was a porter on a truck. On April 17 of this year, after finishing work, Zhou Ruiqing was cleaning the vehicle when he had an argument with Wang Yuchun, a colleague (supervisor). The two sides exchanged rude words, which led to a fight. The result was that the companions persuaded them to separate. Unexpectedly, more than ten days later, Zhou Ruiqing suddenly died. The body of Zhou Ruiqing was sent to the Zhenru Forensic Institute for identification and found to have died from injuries. Wang Yuchun was arrested and the case was prosecuted by Prosecutor Li Fen to the Criminal Court. At 9:00 AM yesterday, Judge Shao Qinzhi opened the court for trial. First, the plaintiff Zhou Shaoting testified about the previous situation and requested a reversal of the verdict and an incidental private prosecution of 1,000 yuan. Next, the detained Wang Yuchun testified, 33 years old, said that there was an argument, but there was no fight. The deceased was standing on the car, cursing at him. Later, he did not know how he fell down and was injured. He was falsely accused of being beaten, and asked for investigation. After the witnesses testified, Prosecutor Li came to the court and made arguments. The debate lasted a long time. The interrogating official considered it to be concluded and scheduled the verdict for the 13th of this month. The defendant's lawyer requested bail. The interrogating official said that the case was of great importance and how could bail be granted? Because of the repeated requests, he was ordered to provide a reliable shop guarantee of 50,000 yuan. If there was no guarantee, he would be remanded in custody.

Woman's Body Found in Huangpu River Case: Court Seems to Have Obtained Clues; Prosecutor Remains Calm, Arrests Three Suspects Yesterday; Deceased Had Borrowed Money from Zhu Fuqing, Currently Involved in Litigation

On the 3rd of this month at 2 PM, when the Taikoo Company's Beiyang-class Shengjing steamship was weighing anchor at Pier No. 3 for departure, the churning of the propellers brought up a female corpse with its lower body naked. Simultaneously, the Water Police Station dispatched detectives to escort a witness (a dock worker) who claimed to have witnessed the deceased being thrown into the Huangpu River by criminals to the court for questioning. This matter has been reported in our newspaper twice. It is now learned that the court, after receiving the report, immediately appointed Prosecutor Xie Lian and Coroner Shen Qijie to the Southern Pier mortuary for an autopsy. The autopsy confirmed that the deceased, Zhang Jinlin, was female, had no trousers on her lower body, and had no visible injuries. Although bluish-purple marks were found on her chest and kidney areas, these were considered normal post-mortem changes and not unusual. Prosecutor Xie Lian, after personally confirming the facts, filled out the death certificate, authorizing the deceased's relative, Zhang Zhou Shi, to arrange for the coffin and burial.

After completing the autopsy, Prosecutor Xie returned to the court and summoned the witness, Hao Zhongyang, to appear in court. After a preliminary investigation, he immediately ordered Chief Judicial Police Officer Zhang Shuping and Chief Police Officer Chen Xihui to lead officers, along with Water Police Station detectives Huang Songsheng, Cheng Yongnian, and Shen Changshan, accompanied by the witness Hao Zhongyang, to calmly proceed to No. 18, Huaixian Lane, Lao Xianqian, in this city, and arrest a woman named Qiao Qi Shi. Then, they proceeded to Qiao Shun Chang Hat Shop on Fangbang Road and arrested Qiao Qi Shi's lover, Qiao Liantang. Finally, they went to

Sipailou and arrested Zhu Fuqing, the owner of Zhu Yuanxing Comb Shop, and three men and women. They were immediately taken to the court, where Prosecutor Xie interrogated them one by one and ordered them to be detained separately for further investigation. All the deceased's belongings were also dispatched by the Water Police Station detectives to the District Court for safekeeping pending collection. It was found that Zhu Fuqing, who was arrested in the case, had borrowed 2,000 yuan from the deceased three years ago, with a written loan agreement. He had recently repaid 260 yuan. The deceased only considered the 260 yuan as interest, while Zhu claimed it was a repayment of the principal and did not

acknowledge it as a loan. He only admitted that the deceased had deposited money in the Zhu Yuanxing Comb Shop. Recently, the deceased, feeling deceived by Zhu Fuqing, published a statement in the newspaper, roughly saying that this loan had been repaid, but the loan agreement had been lost and should be treated as waste paper if found in the future. The deceased then had someone read the draft of the newspaper announcement and realized that she had been deceived by Zhu Fuqing. Subsequently, through introductions, she hired a lawyer and was in the process of filing a lawsuit when the tragedy suddenly occurred, making it suspicious. It is believed that once the court conducts a thorough investigation, the truth will come to light, and the case will soon be fully clarified.

Another "Fire Well" Discovered at the End of Liuying Road in Zhabei Yesterday; Fierce Flames Erupt from Underground Water Pipe; Xinfeng Silk Factory Installs a Pipe to Utilize It as a Furnace

—This is the Sixth "Fire Well" Discovered in This City

Last year, a bizarre "fire well" was discovered in the Taizhou Guild Hall in this city. Recently, a "fire well" also erupted in the manager's residence of the British American Tobacco Company in Western Shanghai. Scientists believe that this phenomenon is worthy of research. According to a report by a Dagong She reporter, a "fire well" has also been discovered in the Xinfeng Silk Weaving Factory on Liuying Road in Zhabei. The reporter visited and inspected the site yesterday afternoon. The details are recorded as follows:

Discovery of the Fire Well The Liansheng Silk Factory at the end of Liuying Road in Zhabei ceased operations last year. Coincidentally, the Xinfeng Silk Weaving Factory in this city was expanding its business and needed to establish a printing and dyeing department. They purchased the land and rebuilt it into a printed fabric dyeing factory. Construction began in December last year, starting with demolition. Recently, workers accidentally discovered a water pipe buried underground, more than ten feet long, from which fierce flames were erupting. The flames were very strong and unapproachable. The factory staff could not extinguish them and covered them with mud and other materials to put out the fire. However, the flames occasionally still burst through, with smoke rising, extremely fierce.

Installation and Utilization The origin of this "fire well" is located next to the factory's finishing room, above which is the third workshop. The factory authorities, seeing the "fire well" continuously emitting flames, decided to utilize the waste. They converted the area into a paint testing laboratory, and the well was connected to a lead pipe that ran directly to the ground. The area around the pipe was paved with cement, leaving only the opening pointing upwards, turning it into a furnace for melting paints. It is also used for cooking, boiling water, and brewing tea. The heating power is equivalent to that of ordinary coal.

Cause of the Fire A Dagong She reporter drove to the site yesterday to observe. The "fire well" is located on the side of the Xinfeng Factory. Outside is a silted small river, with clear water flowing slowly and shadows of trees in the setting sun. However, nearby residents have been dumping trash and debris into the small river, making the river water turbid and emitting a foul odor. When asked, factory personnel said that there was also garbage under the "fire well." Because the land under the well is adjacent to this turbid small river, the amount of garbage is very large. According to geologists, the cause of the fire is the result of garbage decomposition. Because there is much garbage and debris under the well, it contains methane gas, which, after being exposed to the scorching sun, ignites.

Sixth Fire Well It is also learned that the discovery of "fire wells" in Shanghai has occurred six times. The first three times were during the years 1919 and 1920, but the locations and exact times are untraceable. The fourth time was last year in the Taizhou Guild Hall in Xieqiao, where a "fire well" was also discovered. The fire has not been extinguished to this day and is currently used as a fuel source by a soap factory leasing the property. The fifth time was at the end of last month when one was discovered at the residence of the British American Tobacco Company manager on Daxilu. At that time, the fire pipe exploded, and two workers were killed or injured. The sixth time is the "fire well" recorded in this article. Whether the geology of Shanghai contains fire has become a question. It is hoped that scientists and geologists will study this.

Settlement of the Dachunghua Case: Fire Responsibility Not on the Factory Side; Public Safety Department Concludes Interrogation Yesterday

The tragic fire at the Dachunghua Celluloid Factory on Xiaoshadu Road in Western Shanghai, after the families of the victims, Wu Shaowen and 40 others, filed a lawsuit against the factory's chairman, factory manager, deputy manager Zhu Rutang, Ge Tianmin, Jiang Junyan, Sun Hongcheng, Qian Menglin (also known as Qian Zhenhua), etc., has been heard twice by the First Special District Court. Mr. Du Yuesheng, a well-known figure in this city, and lawyer Jin Yu acted as mediators in an effort to reach a peaceful resolution. Both parties have now accepted the mediator's goodwill and agreed on a settlement, bringing the matter to a complete end. As for the case filed by Wu Shaowen and others, yesterday afternoon was another scheduled continuation of the trial. For the sake of solemnity, the police authorities still ordered Huisi Police Station Detective Shang Wu, Deputy Chief Hua, Head Detective Hua, detectives, and several Western detectives to go to the Criminal Court 8 of the First Special Court to assist the bailiffs and maintain order. At half past one, Judge Liu Yugui took the bench with the clerk and immediately declared that the plaintiffs had now submitted a statement requesting the withdrawal of the lawsuit. However, the part of the lawsuit concerning public safety is not legally permitted to be withdrawn and should be investigated and debated. The plaintiff's attorney, upon hearing this, rose and stated that the evidence in the case had not yet been investigated by the plaintiffs and was rather weak. Therefore, they had already requested permission to withdraw the lawsuit and requested that the defendants be acquitted. Judge Liu, because the defendants had not personally appeared, inquired about the cause of the fire and the factory's daily management from their defense attorneys. The defendants' defense attorneys were Xu Jie, Gu Yongquan, and Ling Qihong. Lawyer Xu replied that the fire was caused by the explosion of a stove pot when the neighbors next to the factory were cooking dinner. Not only were the defendants not present at the factory at the time, but all the workers had already left work. It is the factory's rule to stop working at 6 PM every day. Although the raw materials prepared by the factory are easily flammable, they are by no means explosive. The factory does not have electric lights installed and has dozens of fire extinguishers placed throughout the premises. Smoking is strictly prohibited for the workers. Therefore, there is absolutely no risk of fire. Moreover, the Factory Inspection Office and the Fire Brigade send personnel to the factory from time to time to investigate and provide guidance. There has never been any criticism of the management. Therefore, the responsibility for this incident does not lie with the factory, but is due to the carelessness of the neighbors. After the lawyers of both parties concluded their arguments, the court scheduled the verdict for the afternoon of August 13. Thereupon, the Chinese and Western detectives who were in court also withdrew.

Robbery of a Bank on Jinling Road: Summary of the Criminals' Confessions; He Jichang Initiated the Crime; All Criminals Admitted in Their Confessions

After the robbery of the Bank of Communications car on Jinling Road in Zhabei on the morning of the 2nd of this month, Lu Ying, the chief of the Municipal Public Security Bureau's Detective General Team, and Ji Yuanpu, the deputy chief, immediately ordered Bao Ziying, the chief of the Xinzha Detective Branch, and Shi Zuhan and Chu Jingwu, the deputy chiefs, to lead detectives to crack the gang of thieves within three days and arrest 23 male and female suspects and a ten-year-old girl. This has already been reported in this newspaper. It is now learned that

the confessions of the thieves have been clarified as follows: (1) He Jichang (nicknamed "Little Shandong") confessed, "I committed a crime in the French Concession before and served a five-year sentence. Later, I was released in a general amnesty. A month ago, I met Bu Jinyuan, who said there was a deal, that the Bank of Communications car often passed through Jinling Road. So I invited Zhang Caihu and six others to gather in the Caojiadu workshop. There were two pistols and one Mauser pistol. The Bank of Communications guard's gun was seized by Xu Axiang. After the robbery, we went to the Zhaofeng

Garden to divide the loot. I got 70 yuan." (2) Lu Jinfu confessed, "A week ago, Little Shandong invited me to Jinling Road to rob. We set off from Little Shandong's house. Bu Jinyuan carried the Mauser pistol, my brother and Shi Arong each carried a pistol. We told Xu Axiang to push the bamboo cart ahead of us to wait on Jinling Road. The police's gun was seized when Shi Arong held the gun against the policeman, and Xu Axiang snatched the gun. Afterwards, I got 40 yuan." (3) Zhang Jichuan confessed, "A month ago, Little Shandong invited me and said they had pistols and a Mauser pistol, and we would rob. He took me to Jinling Road to take a look. I went with Li Dean, who

was in charge of watching the car driver (referring to the Bank of Communications car driver). Later, Li and I divided 7,500 yuan, and I used 40 yuan." (4) Lu Jintao confessed, "I was called by Zhang Caihu. There were seven of us who went that day. I got 30 yuan. There were more than 20 people who shared the loot. The police guard's gun was seized from He Jichang's house." (5) Zhang Yansheng confessed, "I didn't know they were going to rob, but He Jichang and I are friends. He came to my house to play, and he put the pistol and banknotes in my house. I didn't know they were stolen." (6) Xu Axiang confessed, "On the day of the robbery, Zhang Caihu called me at my house and said he had a small cart of bamboo and told me to push it to Jinling Road and stop. Later, a car came, and they told me to turn the cart

over across the road and rush up to rob. Later, Zhang Caihu gave me 30 yuan. I only used seven yuan, and the remaining 23 yuan has been confiscated. Lu Jintao took the guard's pistol, etc." (7) Shi Arong confessed, "On the day of the gun, I saw Little Shandong in a teahouse in Caojiadu. He told me to go rob with him. We gathered at his house

and set off. When we robbed on Jinling Road, I held a pistol against the policeman, and Lu Jinfu seized the policeman's gun. After the robbery, we took a car to Zhaofeng Garden, and Little Shandong gave me 30 yuan." (8) Li Dean confessed, "Zhang Caihu called me and Lin Gen to guard someone on Zhongshan Road (referring to Liu Defa, the driver of the Feili Automobile Company), and gave me a pistol. I said I didn't know how to use the pistol. Later, Zhang Caihu gave me 30 yuan." (9) Bu Jinyuan confessed,

"Wang Kaifu told Sun Laoer about the case, Sun Laoer told me, and I discussed it with Little Shandong. At first, Little Shandong said someone didn't have a gun, so I contacted Sun Laoer and spent over 100 yuan. Later, after the robbery, He Jichang gave me 50 yuan and gave me 690 yuan to give to Wang Kaifu 560 yuan. Sun Laoer used 60 yuan, and the remaining 70 yuan has been taken by others. Wang Kaifu's 560 yuan included 150 yuan for three guns and 300 yuan for tips" (referring to the person who first initiated the robbery of the Bank of Communications). (10) Wang Kaifu confessed, "A month ago, I told Zhou Xiaolao Han that the Bank of Communications car

was transporting banknotes and often traveled on Jinling Road. As a result, Bu Jinyuan and his gang went there. They said they robbed 700 or 800 yuan, which was not enough for carfare, etc." (11) Zhou Yiling (Zhou Xiaolao Han) confessed, "I sell yellow sand and gravel, run a teahouse, and don't do bad things." (12) Lu Caiji confessed, "I am already 60 years old. Lu Jintao and Lu Jinfu are my sons, Lu Chen Shi is my daughter-in-law, Lu Chunshou is my nephew, and Xu Atao is my son-in-law. I don't know they are doing bad things," etc. (13) Xu He Shi confessed,

"I met Xu Sanbao (referring to Xu Axiang) in a brothel, and he paid 1,000 yuan to redeem me," etc. (14) Hou Gu Shi confessed, "My husband has been dead for many years, and I have no one to rely on, so I am living with Zhang Yansheng." (15) Lu Zhao Shi confessed, "My husband is also dead, so I am living with Lu Xisheng (at large). I don't know what he does." The remaining Ding Lan Jin, Mao Shoubao, etc. all have confessions, all of which are evasive. The confessions of the above-mentioned thieves and male and female suspects are all very long. The above is a summary.

Two Years After Yao Shenqing's Death, Son of Concubine Files Suit, Requesting Confirmation of Identity, Court Orders Both Parties to Mediate

Yao Shenqing, former compradore of Anli & Co., died in 1933, leaving behind a considerable estate. The estate was inherited by his wife, Sun Shi, and sons, Boxiong, Yanqing, Zimin, Yingjun, and Zhijie. Recently, Yao Fuzeng claimed to be the son of Shenqing's concubine, but the Yao family refused to recognize him. Therefore, he hired lawyers Huang Shaochang and Ling Qihong to file a lawsuit against Yao Sun Shi, Yao Boxiong, and Yao Yanqing in the First Special District Court to confirm his identity. The First Special Court has summoned them to court to encourage mediation. This was reported in this newspaper on the 12th of last month. Yesterday morning, Judge Peng Shi opened the Fourth Civil Court to continue the hearing. The defendants were not present, and lawyer Cai Liucheng represented them. Of the three witnesses summoned, Zhou Ahua, Yao Tiqing, and Zhang Chuchen, only Zhou Ahua appeared in court. According to his testimony, the plaintiff was born to Jin Shi, Yao Boxiong's nanny, and was adopted by Yao Shenqing. Later, the plaintiff married into the Tang family, and I introduced him to the Tang family on his behalf. The plaintiff's lawyer argued that the defendants must be present in court because, in this type of personal lawsuit, there is much to be learned from the expressions and demeanor of the parties. He also requested that blood tests be conducted by a forensic doctor, which would make it easy to determine the truth. The defendants' lawyer also presented a copy of Yao Shenqing's obituary and a copy of Shenqing's mother's obituary, neither of which listed the plaintiff, to prove that the plaintiff was not Shenqing's biological son. Judge Peng believed that the witnesses in the case had not all arrived and that it was necessary for the defendants to appear in court in person. Therefore, he ordered the hearing to be postponed and again urged the parties to attempt mediation outside of court.

At 1:00 AM yesterday morning, nine bandits suddenly went to rob the Liang family at No. 27, Lane 88, Changping Road in Western Shanghai. Two of the bandits were armed with pistols. They tricked their way into opening the front door and went straight into the store, loudly asking if Mr. Liang was at home. At that time, the owner of the house had not yet gone to bed. Upon hearing the commotion downstairs, he knew something was wrong. He groped his way downstairs, went out through the back door, circled to the front door, and peeked in to see what was happening. When he saw the bandits, he immediately turned around and ran out of the lane, shouting for help. As a result, the bandits inside the house did not have time to search thoroughly and simply grabbed three quilts and fled. At that time, a peddler from Jiangbei named Yu Chengbin, 57 years old, happened to be at the entrance of the lane. When he saw the bandits running out, he immediately rushed to chase them out of a sense of righteousness. Unexpectedly, the bandits noticed and fired two shots at Wang, hitting both of his legs. He immediately fell to the ground. The Gordon Road Police Station was notified and sent detectives to the scene, but the bandits had already fled. They quickly took Wang Chengbin to the hospital for treatment, but because of his advanced age, his condition was very critical. Minfeng Paper Company Obtains Exclusive Manufacturing Rights for Cigarette Paper

Minfeng Paper Company, founded by Chu Huiseng, Du Yuesheng, Jin Tingsun, Zhu Meixian, Jin Runxiang, etc., has been in operation for many years and is located in Jiaxing. It has been imitating various foreign paper products, offering high-quality goods at reasonable prices, and has been widely praised by society. Last year, the company's management, in view of the large amount of imported cigarette paper, proposed to add investment to purchase machinery for imitation production. After submitting the proposal to the shareholders' meeting, it was resolved and approved. Furthermore, because no domestic manufacturer was producing this cigarette paper, it applied to the government for exclusive manufacturing rights in accordance with the Industrial Encouragement Law. It has recently been learned that the Ministry of Industry has approved the application. The notice from the Ministry of Industry received by the company yesterday stated that the company's application to use the latest foreign methods to imitate cigarette paper and to grant exclusive manufacturing rights had been reviewed by the Industrial Encouragement Review Committee. The ministry re-examined the results and found that it complied with the provisions of Article 1, Section 2 of the Industrial Encouragement Law. It was approved to enjoy exclusive manufacturing rights for five years, from September 1, 1935, to August 31, 1940, in the four provinces of Zhejiang, Fujian, Shandong, and Hebei, and in the three municipalities of Shanghai, Tianjin, and Qingdao. Please pay the stamp tax of 1 yuan and 50 cents to issue the license. This is a notice. It is also reported that the machines ordered by the company have been continuously arriving at the factory and are being installed as quickly as possible. It is expected that the products will be available in March or April next spring, which is also a dawn for the domestic goods industry.

Shanghai National Products Company; The National Products Association Will Provide Legal Protection for Unpaid Consignment Payments Owed to Various Domestic Goods Factories

The Shanghai Citizens' National Products Promotion Association has repeatedly received visits from factory members, including Xu Yunhui, a representative of the Senyuanxiang Jewelry Factory, and letters from more than 20 companies, including the Dachunghua Celluloid Factory, requesting protection for the priority interest in outstanding consignment payments and inventory for products consigned to the Shanghai National Products Company, to avoid innocent losses, and requesting leadership in negotiations. After deliberation by the Standing Committee, it was resolved to strive for protection in accordance with the provisions of Article 6, Section 5 of Chapter 2 of the Association's charter. However, it was unclear whether consignment payments were treated differently from ordinary outstanding payments, so a letter was sent to the Municipal Chamber of Commerce for interpretation and legal negotiation, and the matter was recorded. It is now learned that the Association's Secretariat yesterday issued a notice to all factory members, soliciting information on outstanding consignment payments and inventory owed by the company in order to compile a summary of the case, nominate responsible representatives, and entrust legal advisors Xue Dubi, Pan Zhensheng, Mao Yun, Ma Junshuo, Bao Zhenhuang, and other senior lawyers to handle the case. The original letter to the Municipal Chamber of Commerce is excerpted below: "To the esteemed Chamber: This is to report that the Shanghai National Products Company, as the earliest established store dedicated to promoting domestic goods, advocated cooperation between production and sales and consolidated production and construction. It held unlimited hopes for a prosperous future. Unfortunately, due to the collapse of the rural economy and the decline in social consumption, it suffered from financial difficulties and was unable to maintain operations. Faced with the environment, it suddenly suspended operations, ultimately unable to reorganize and declared liquidation, which has severely affected the promotion of domestic goods and is of particular concern to the rights of various factories. The association has received visits from members of more than ten factories, including the Senyuanxiang Jewelry Factory, and letters from more than twenty factories, including the Dachunghua Celluloid Factory, requesting protection for the priority interest in outstanding consignment payments and promissory notes for consigned products. In this regard, the association has found that it has no basis to determine whether consignment payments, payments for purchased goods, matured promissory notes, and unmatured promissory notes (using the company's suspension of operations as the standard date) are treated differently in the event of the company's declaration of liquidation. Therefore, this letter is sent to you with the hope that you will provide a legal interpretation so that we may proceed accordingly. We thank you in advance.

Large Quantity of Red Pills Seized at North Station, Four People Involved Arrested, All Employees of Huitong Company, Yesterday Taken to Public Security Bureau for Interrogation

At around 10 AM on the 3rd of this month, military police stationed at the North Railway Station were inspecting passengers entering and leaving the station to check for smuggled contraband. They noticed several people carrying two large wooden boxes, intending to transport them to Xin'an County, Luoyang, Henan. The military police, as per regulations, ordered them to stop and open the boxes for inspection. Unexpectedly, the large wooden boxes had false bottoms. The top was filled with towels, galoshes, and other items, with a tin box hidden in the middle, and dozens of pounds of red pills, estimated at over 600,000 pills, were concealed in the box and the false bottoms. The people transporting the items, realizing the gravity of the situation, immediately fled, failing to be apprehended. Only the red pills, along with the two large wooden boxes, were taken to the railway police station for detailed investigation. It was then learned that the wooden boxes were being shipped by the Huitong Transportation Company at 175 Jielu Road, and that the Huitong Company's warehouse office was located at 799 Qiujiang Road, Zhabei. The military police immediately dispatched personnel to investigate. However, the warehouse office was tightly locked, with no one inside. Subsequently, Fang Jianquan, the accountant of Huitong Transportation Company, was summoned to the police station for questioning. According to Fang, although the boxes were shipped by their company, the company was unaware of the contents and that there were contraband items in the boxes. To his knowledge, the boxes were directly entrusted to the company office for shipment by Wang Shanqing, who lived at No. 26 Fudeli, North Sichuan Road. Therefore, the office should be responsible for the matter. The police station then ordered Fang to investigate. At 4:25 PM the day before yesterday, Fang found Wang Chengyu, an accountant from Suzhou in the company's accounting department, along with Pan Lansheng from Qingpu, the director of the Huitong warehouse office, and clerks Ye Buyuan and Yao Zuozhou (both from Suzhou) hiding at No. 9 Ningkangli, 381 North Zhejiang Road. He reported this to the Railway Police Department, which notified the Municipal Public Security Bureau to send detectives, together with Chinese Detective Shang Wu and Bao Detective Zhuge Qian from the Huisi Police Station, and Western Detective Locke, to the address. They apprehended Wang Chengyu and the other three and took them to the Huisi Police Station for detention. Yesterday morning, they were escorted to the Eighth Criminal Court of the First Special District Court. Detective Wang Zhengrong from the Public Security Bureau brought a document requesting their transfer. Qian Jiujiu, the lawyer for the police station, explained the case in detail and did not oppose the transfer. Subsequently, Fang Jianquan, the accountant of Huitong Transportation Company, stated that the boxes were received by Pan Lansheng, the director of their company's office. Pan had been whispering with Wang Chengyu in the company for a long time on the 2nd of this month, and the four of them were arrested together yesterday, suggesting a conspiracy. The company was unaware of the matter. Among those arrested, Wang was an accountant, while the other three were employees of the office. When questioned, Pan Lansheng confessed that the boxes were sent by someone in a rickshaw on August 2nd, claiming they contained towels and galoshes to be shipped to Xin'an County, Luoyang. Yao Zuozhou weighed the boxes at the time, and Yao and Ye Buyuan transported them to the North Railway Station, unaware that they contained red pills. The other three gave evasive answers. Judge Wu Zehan reviewed the confessions and approved the transfer of Wang Chengyu and the other three to the Shanghai Municipal Public Security Bureau for further interrogation.

District Court Rectifies Conduct

The Shanghai District Court issued a proclamation yesterday, the text of which is transcribed below: "The court's handling of affairs places the utmost importance on conduct. Shanghai is a mixed community of Chinese and foreigners, with both good and bad elements. It is inevitable that unscrupulous individuals will fabricate lawsuits and seek to profit by exploiting them. Some may even falsely claim to be acquainted with court personnel, falsely enter and leave the court, in order to achieve their fraudulent wishes. The ignorant are deceived by them and believe them to be true. After regretting it, they file anonymous complaints, making reckless attacks, often concealing the facts, making it impossible to investigate. Since assuming office, the president of this court has been supervising at all times, without any leniency. Therefore, this proclamation is issued earnestly. It must be known that this court accepts civil and criminal lawsuits and handles them in accordance with the law, based on evidence. If there are unscrupulous individuals who swindle and deceive others, or impersonate court staff to defraud and obtain money, the victims should immediately seize them on the spot, or identify them by name and report the facts. If court staff are found to have engaged in illegal activities, they may also be accused. Once the facts are verified, they will be severely punished. However, anonymous letters and arbitrary accusations will not be accepted. All must comply. This is hereby proclaimed."

Huidefeng Sinking, St. Arping Iron Barge Successfully Salvaged

Since the Huidefeng large tugboat, the St. Arping, collided with the China Merchants Bureau's Jiangshun Wheel and sank in the Pujiang River, the tugboat, which cost over 200,000 yuan to build, has been undergoing salvage operations, despite having extensive insurance coverage. After days of salvage work, the sunken barge's hull has been dragged closer to the shore by two large tugboats. Divers and technicians are now being sent into the water to repair the breaches. After the water in each cabin is pumped out, it can be floated to the surface of the river and towed to the shipyard for major repairs.

Bank Inspection Report Compilation

The 242nd Inspection Report on the Issuance Reserve of Central Bank Exchange Vouchers states: "In accordance with the provisions of Article 13 of the Central Bank Law, this committee is responsible for inspecting the number of exchange vouchers issued by this bank and the reserve funds. The 241st inspection was held at the Issuance Bureau of this bank on August 3, 1935. The results of the inspection are reported as follows: (A) The total amount of exchange vouchers issued is 107,683,113 silver dollars, including 100,757,743 silver dollar vouchers and 6,925,370 fractional currency vouchers. The total amount of exchange voucher reserves is 107,683,113 silver dollars, including cash reserve of 83,483,113 silver dollars. This cash reserve includes 78,336,148 silver dollars stored in this bank's issuance vault, 1,300,416 silver dollars stored in branches in various ports, and 2,846,549 silver dollars deposited with other banks. The guarantee reserve is equivalent to 24,200,000 silver dollars. (B) The total amount of customs gold exchange vouchers issued is 372,324.7 yuan. The total amount of customs gold exchange voucher reserves is 373,324.7 yuan. This reserve includes 7,351 taels, 9 mace, and 5 fen of bullion, valued at 5.0779, equivalent to 373,124.5 customs gold. According to Article 22 of the Central Bank Law, the cash reserve must be at least 60%, and the remainder must be guaranteed by legal guarantees. The results of this inspection show that the cash reserve exceeds 60%, and the guarantee reserve is within 40%, which is in compliance with the law. This is hereby reported. August 5, 1935, Li Fuxun, Chairman of the Board of Supervisors of the Central Bank, Supervisors Xie Mengjun, Bei Songsun, Qin Runqing, Lu Qiaqing, Lin Kanghou, Xu Jiyi."

The Four Banks Joint Reserve Vault is jointly established by the Salt, Yanye, Jincheng, Zhongnan, and Continental Banks, specializing in issuing Zhongnan Bank banknotes. According to the vault's issuance regulations, banknotes are issued with sufficient reserves. The cash reserve is at least 60%, and the guarantee reserve is at most 40%. A public notice is issued every week, and it is audited by the auditors and accountants of the four banks. The following is a transcript of the 292nd public notice of the Shanghai Reserve Vault on August 3, 1935: The amount of banknotes in circulation is 19,842,573 yuan. The total amount of reserves is 19,842,573 yuan, including cash reserve of 17,741,893 yuan and guarantee reserve of 2,100,680 yuan.
